//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Ellipse_sign_115.svg/62px-Ellipse_sign_115.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090301125733/http://www.aguadilla.gobierno.pr/">aguadilla.gobierno.pr</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Aguadilla</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;a\xc9\xa3wa\xcb\x88\xc3\xb0i\xca\x9da&#93;</a></span>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991"><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">locally</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;awa\xcb\x88\xc3\xb0i\xca\x9da&#93;</a></span>), founded in 1775 by Luis de C\xc3\xb3rdova, is a <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguadilla barrio-pueblo">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> located in the northwestern tip of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the north and west, north of <a href="/wiki/Aguada,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguada, Puerto Rico">Aguada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moca,_Puerto_Rico" title="Moca, Puerto Rico">Moca</a> and west of <a href="/wiki/Isabela,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isabela, Puerto Rico">Isabela</a>. Aguadilla is spread over 15 <i>barrios</i> and <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguadilla barrio-pueblo">Aguadilla Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city). It is a principal city and core of the <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla-Isabela-San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Aguadilla-Isabela-San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Metropolitan Statistical Area">Aguadilla-Isabela-San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology_and_nicknames">Etymology and nicknames</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ojo_de_Agua_1_-_Aguadilla_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ojo_de_Agua_1_-_Aguadilla_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Ojo_de_Agua_1_-_Aguadilla_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ojo_de_Agua_1_-_Aguadilla_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Ojo_de_Agua_1_-_Aguadilla_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ojo_de_Agua_1_-_Aguadilla_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Ojo_de_Agua_1_-_Aguadilla_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/El_Parterre" title="El Parterre"><i>Ojo de Agua</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)" title="Spring (hydrology)">water spring</a> located in downtown (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">pueblo</i></span>), which gives the municipality one of its nicknames</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Aguadilla is a shortening of the town\'s original name <i>San Carlos de La Aguadilla</i>. The name <i>Aguadilla</i> is a diminutive of <i><a href="/wiki/Aguada,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguada, Puerto Rico">Aguada</a></i>, which is the name of the <a href="/wiki/Aguada_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguada barrio-pueblo">town</a> and municipality located to the south. Some of the municipality\'s nicknames are: <i>Jard\xc3\xadn del Atl\xc3\xa1ntico</i> ("Garden of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a>"), <i>Pueblo de los Tiburones</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">Shark</a> Town") and <i>La Villa del <a href="/wiki/El_Parterre" title="El Parterre">Ojo de Agua</a></i> ("Villa of the <a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)" title="Spring (hydrology)">Water Spring</a>") after the natural water spring that was used by early settlers and Spanish soldiers as a water source which is now located in <a href="/wiki/El_Parterre" title="El Parterre">El Parterre Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguadilla barrio-pueblo">Aguadilla Pueblo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>According to sources, a <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> settlement called <i>Aymam\xc3\xb3n</i> was located close to the <a href="/wiki/Culebrinas_River" title="Culebrinas River">Culebrinas River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The present territory of Aguadilla was originally part of the territory of <a href="/wiki/Aguada,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguada, Puerto Rico">Aguada</a>. In 1775, the foundation of Aguadilla by Don Luis de C\xc3\xb3rdova was approved.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> But it was not until 1780 that the territory was properly segregated, making the founding of the town official. Originally, Aguadilla was constituted by the <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Victoria, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Victoria</a> and Hig\xc3\xbcey barrios.<sup id="cite_ref-enciclopediapr_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enciclopediapr-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This region was already inhabited and known as Aguadilla before 1770. In 1776, <a href="/wiki/Fray_%C3%8D%C3%B1igo_Abbad_y_Lasierra" title="Fray \xc3\x8d\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra">Fray \xc3\x8d\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra</a> in his description of the towns of the island, mentioned it as the "new Town of <b>San Carlos de La Aguadilla</b>." Nevertheless, according to Dr. <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_Stahl" title="Agust\xc3\xadn Stahl">Agust\xc3\xadn Stahl</a> in his <i>Foundation of Aguadilla</i>, it was not until 1780 that the town was officially founded. The construction of a new church and the proceedings to become an independent village began in 1775.<sup id="cite_ref-El_Castillo_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_Castillo-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The population in the Village of Aguadilla continued to increase constantly mainly due to its excellent port and strategic location in the route of the boats. In 1776, when <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> became independent for the first time, the loyalists of <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">Spanish descent</a> emigrated to Puerto Rico, mainly to Aguadilla, which caused the population to continue increasing significantly. In 1831, according to Don Pedro Tom\xc3\xa1s de C\xc3\xb3rdova, the area or "party" of Aguadilla belonged to Aguada. At this time, the territorial organization of Aguadilla was as follows: Pueblo Norte (North Town), Pueblo Sur (South Town), Ceiba Alta, Ceiba Baja, Monta\xc3\xb1a, Malezas, Aguacate, Dos Palmas, Camaseyes, Plainela, Borinquen, Arenales, Hig\xc3\xbcey, Corrales, Victoria, and Mangual.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Don Pedro Tom\xc3\xa1s de C\xc3\xb3rdova mentions the road of Aguadilla formed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Punta_Borinquen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Punta Borinquen (page does not exist)">Punta Borinquen</a> and San Francisco, as the "anchorage of the ships that travel from Europe to <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>". He adds that its "port is the most frequented in the Island due to the proportions that it offers to refresh all class of ship."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 1860, Aguadilla was officially declared a village.<sup id="cite_ref-enciclopediapr_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enciclopediapr-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Several years later, when the island was territorially organized into seven departments, Aguadilla became the head of the third department that included the municipalities of Aguada, <a href="/wiki/Isabela,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isabela, Puerto Rico">Isabela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lares,_Puerto_Rico" title="Lares, Puerto Rico">Lares</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moca,_Puerto_Rico" title="Moca, Puerto Rico">Moca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinc%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Rinc\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Rinc\xc3\xb3n</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a>. In January 1841 a Royal Order transferred the judicial party from Aguada to Aguadilla. In 1878, according to Don Manuel Ebeda y Delgado, the territorial organization of Aguadilla had varied a little. At this time Plainela, Hig\xc3\xbcey, and Mangual barrios are not mentioned. The Dos Palmas barrio appears as Palmar. Also at this time, three new barrios are mentioned: Guerrero, Caimital Alto, and Caimital Bajo. In 1898, even with the change of sovereignty in the island, the territorial organization of Aguadilla is the same to that of 1878. Nevertheless, in the Census of 1899, downtown Aguadilla appears constituted by Hig\xc3\xbcey, Iglesia, Nueva, Santa Barbara, and Tamarindo barrios. Malezas barrio appears subdivided into Maleza Alta and Maleza Baja. From that time, the territorial organization of Aguadilla did not change, until 1948, when the Puerto Rico Department of Planning prepared the map of the city and its barrios, and following instructions of city authorities, Hig\xc3\xbcey and parts of Caimital Alto barrios are annexed to <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguadilla barrio-pueblo">Downtown Aguadilla</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ramey_Air_Force_Base">Ramey Air Force Base</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ramey Air Force Base"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:FAA_radar_tower_in_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/FAA_radar_tower_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-FAA_radar_tower_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/FAA_radar_tower_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-FAA_radar_tower_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/FAA_radar_tower_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-FAA_radar_tower_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="5184" /></a><figcaption>FAA radar tower in Aguadilla, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Aguadilla was the site of the U.S. military\'s <a href="/wiki/Ramey_Air_Force_Base" title="Ramey Air Force Base">Ramey Air Force Base</a> for almost five decades. During this period, Aguadilla was home to the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Air_Command" title="Strategic Air Command">Strategic Air Command</a>, equipped with <a href="/wiki/RB-36" class="mw-redirect" title="RB-36">RB-36s</a> and <a href="/wiki/72d_Bombardment_Wing,_Heavy" class="mw-redirect" title="72d Bombardment Wing, Heavy">72d Bombardment Wing, Heavy</a> equipped with <a href="/wiki/B-52" class="mw-redirect" title="B-52">B-52s</a>, an important strategic facility during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.\nActivated in June 1952 as a&#160;Strategic Air Command&#160;very long-range reconnaissance unit at&#160;Ramey AFB,&#160;Puerto Rico, but not operational until October 1952. Redesignated as&#160;72d Strategic Reconnaissance Wing&#160;and received 3 (60th, 73rd and 301st) squadrons of&#160;RB-36D/E/F/H Peacemaker bombers. Also, the 915th Air Rescue Squadron. Conducted global strategic reconnaissance 1953\xe2\x80\x931955, gradually shifting to a bombardment training mission beginning in 1954, being upgraded to B-36J and B-36J(III) Featherweights by 1955. Redesignated&#160;72d Bombardment Wing&#160;in 1958. \nWith the phaseout of the B-36s in 1958, received&#160;B-52G Stratofortress&#160;intercontinental strategic bombers.\n</p><p>Though the infrastructure still exists, the airport was handed over to the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">Government of Puerto Rico</a> in 1973. The aerial facilities are now controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Ports_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Ports Authority">Puerto Rico Ports Authority</a> and comprise the <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Hern%C3%A1ndez_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez International Airport">Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez International Airport</a>. The barracks now host the Faro Inn Suites, a 79-room hotel. The Officer\'s Club now hosts the Faro Conference Center, a 22,000-square-foot (2,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) meeting facility. The hospital is now the Courtyard by <a href="/wiki/Marriott_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Marriott Hotels &amp; Resorts">Marriott</a> Punta Borinquen Resort &amp; Casino,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a 150-room hotel with a casino and the first Marriott in Puerto Rico outside of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> Metropolitan Area.\n</p><p>Ramey also hosts the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Aguadilla" title="University of Puerto Rico at Aguadilla">University of Puerto Rico at Aguadilla</a> and the Friedrich Froebel Bilingual School (K-9).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The high school became Ramey Job Corps Campus<sup id="cite_ref-Ramey.jobcorps.gov_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramey.jobcorps.gov-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the elementary school became the Esther Feliciano Mendoza Middle School. Centro de Adiestramiento y Bellas Artes (CABA) since 1979 has been the only public school of arts in Puerto Rico (7\xe2\x80\x9312). Ramey is also the site of the new Ramey Skating Park and a new <i>mariposario</i> (butterfly farm) and the Ramey Shopping Center.\n</p><p>There is still an active part of the base that hosts the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a> Borinquen Air Station. There are also other government agencies based at Ramey, including the United States <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">U.S. Customs &amp; Border Protection\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Air_and_Marine" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of Air and Marine">Office of Air and Marine</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Border_Patrol" title="United States Border Patrol">Office of Border Patrol</a>, the <i>Fuerzas Unidas de R\xc3\xa1pida Acci\xc3\xb3n</i> (United Forces for Rapid Action) of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Police Department">Puerto Rico Police Department</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard" title="Puerto Rico National Guard">Puerto Rico National Guard</a>.\n</p><p>There is also a post office, the <i>Centro de Servicios al Conductor</i> (Driver\'s Services Center), a bakery, and a <a href="/wiki/Banco_Popular_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Banco Popular de Puerto Rico">Banco Popular de Puerto Rico</a> location.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="San_Antonio">San Antonio</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: San Antonio"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguadilla_Plaza,_Puerto_Rico,_1910.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Aguadilla_Plaza%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1910.JPG/200px-Aguadilla_Plaza%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1910.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Aguadilla_Plaza%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1910.JPG/300px-Aguadilla_Plaza%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1910.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Aguadilla_Plaza%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1910.JPG/400px-Aguadilla_Plaza%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1910.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2155" data-file-height="1548" /></a><figcaption>Aguadilla in 1910</figcaption></figure>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236091366">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid .mbox-image-div{width:52px}html.client-js body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Special:EditPage/Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>San Antonio village was established in the mid-19th century. It was populated by 60 families. Originally the place where these families were located was known as <i>Bajura de Vadi</i>, the place later to become known as San Antonio.\n</p><p>In 1918, as a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/1918_San_Ferm%C3%ADn_earthquake" title="1918 San Ferm\xc3\xadn earthquake">1918 San Ferm\xc3\xadn earthquake</a>, the village was completely destroyed by a <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a>. The families suffered the struggles caused by this natural disaster due by the proximity of the village to the shore.\n</p><p>The residents of the village decided re-localize the village in a higher area further from shore. The new location was what today is known as <a href="/wiki/Ramey_Air_Force_Base" title="Ramey Air Force Base">Ramey</a>.\n</p><p>The village\'s infrastructure started its evolution. Luis R. Esteves and Juan Garcia established the first two theaters in the area. A new was social club form, known as "Luz del Porvenir" (Light of the Future). A new school system was the pride of the village because it offered them the opportunity to give their children an education without having to go 9 miles (14&#160;km) south downtown. There was also a new bakery and a post office, among other facilities. At this time, the village also began its Patron Festival.\n</p><p>The clothing industry was a major source of employment.\n</p><p>In September 1939, some 3,796 acres (15.4&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) covered by sugar cane, was expropriated for the military at the cost of $1,215,000, in order to build an air base that came to be known as <a href="/wiki/Ramey_Air_Force_Base" title="Ramey Air Force Base">Ramey Air Force Base</a>.\n</p><p>Since the foundation, the village has suffered three expropriations as a result of expansions to <a href="/wiki/Ramey_Air_Force_Base" title="Ramey Air Force Base">Ramey Air Force Base</a>. These expropriations delayed and ended the plans to turn San Antonio into a town.\n</p><p>Today, the population of San Antonio consists of approximately ten thousand people. It has a modern square, a <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police" title="Puerto Rico Police">Puerto Rico State Police</a> Station, a coliseum, an industrial park, public housing, a baseball park, a public school system, shops, and many other characteristics of a small town. The town also has a flag and an emblem. Roberto Rom\xc3\xa1n Acevedo designed the town flag and emblem.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tragedy_on_election_day_in_1944">Tragedy on election day in 1944</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tragedy on election day in 1944"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sign_for_former_train_station,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sign_for_former_train_station%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/150px-Sign_for_former_train_station%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sign_for_former_train_station%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/225px-Sign_for_former_train_station%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sign_for_former_train_station%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/300px-Sign_for_former_train_station%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a><figcaption>Sign at former train stop in Aguadilla</figcaption></figure>\n<p>On the early morning hours of November 7, 1944, Puerto Rico suffered the worst railroad accident in its history.<sup id="cite_ref-endi_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endi-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Train No. 3 was traveling from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> carrying passengers to their hometowns for the island general elections being held that same day. It stopped at the Jim\xc3\xa9nez Station in Aguadilla for a routine <a href="/wiki/Railroad_engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Railroad engineer">engineer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fireman_(steam_engine)" title="Fireman (steam engine)">boilerman</a> exchange with Train No. 4, which was heading to San Juan. The engineer assigned to Train No. 3\'s ride from Jim\xc3\xa9nez Station to Ponce was Jos\xc3\xa9 Antonio Rom\xc3\xa1n, an experienced freight train engineer who had never worked on passenger trains.<sup id="cite_ref-endi_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endi-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When the train left the station at 2:00 am, it comprised 6 passenger cars with hundreds of passengers and two freight cars.\n</p>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuesta_Vieja,_street_in_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Cuesta_Vieja%2C_street_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/150px-Cuesta_Vieja%2C_street_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="105" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Cuesta_Vieja%2C_street_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/225px-Cuesta_Vieja%2C_street_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Cuesta_Vieja%2C_street_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/300px-Cuesta_Vieja%2C_street_in_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="424" /></a><figcaption><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cuesta Vieja</i></span>, a sector of Aguadilla, where the train derailed</figcaption></figure>\n<p>At 2:20&#160;a.m. the train started to descend a hill section in Aguadilla known as <i>Cuesta Vieja</i> (Old Hill) at, what some witnesses described as, excessive speed. When the train reached the leveling-off point at the bottom of the hill it <a href="/wiki/Derailment" title="Derailment">derailed</a>. The steam locomotive ran into a ditch, where it exploded, and one of the freight cars crashed into one of the passenger cars, killing many inside. Witnesses described the scene as horrendous, with some accounts stating that parents were throwing their children out the windows to save them from the wreckage.<sup id="cite_ref-endi_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endi-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Chief of Police Guillermo Arroyo stated that the locomotive (No. 72), the express car, and three second class passenger cars were completely destroyed. Oscar Valle, an Aguadilla correspondent to <i><a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Puerto_Rico)" title="El Mundo (Puerto Rico)">El Mundo</a></i> newspaper, summarized the scene with: "The locomotive suffered a terrible explosion as it derailed, and the impact was so strong that 3 passenger cars were converted into a fantastic mound of wreckage".<sup id="cite_ref-endi_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endi-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the end, 16 passengers lost their lives, including the engineer and the boilerman, and 50 were injured in the crash.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hurricane_Maria">Hurricane Maria</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hurricane Maria"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:170923-H-NI589-0009_(23543368528).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/170923-H-NI589-0009_%2823543368528%29.jpg/220px-170923-H-NI589-0009_%2823543368528%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/170923-H-NI589-0009_%2823543368528%29.jpg/330px-170923-H-NI589-0009_%2823543368528%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/170923-H-NI589-0009_%2823543368528%29.jpg/440px-170923-H-NI589-0009_%2823543368528%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a><figcaption>Aerial view of Aguadilla a few days after Hurricane Maria</figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck Puerto Rico on September 20, 2017, causing large-scale damage and destruction to infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In Aguadilla 10 inches of rain were recorded and its more than 54,000 residents were left with no electrical power.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The four radar systems used by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> for flights in and around Puerto Rico were damaged by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>, and it took nearly two weeks to fix them. One of the radar systems is located in Aguadilla.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Aguadilla is located in the northwest coast of the island of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, in the Western Coastal Plains. It is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> in the north, the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Isabela,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isabela, Puerto Rico">Isabela</a> on the east, and <a href="/wiki/Moca,_Puerto_Rico" title="Moca, Puerto Rico">Moca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aguada,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguada, Puerto Rico">Aguada</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_General_Info_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_General_Info-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The area of the municipality is 35.5 square miles. It is mostly plain, with some notable hills being Jim\xc3\xa9nez (728 feet) and Vi\xc3\xb1et (689 feet). It has only one river, the <a href="/wiki/Culebrinas_River" title="Culebrinas River">Culebrinas</a>, which separates Aguadilla from Aguada. Also, Cedro Creek which separates Aguadilla from Isabela in the north.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_General_Info_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_General_Info-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1103" data-file-height="886" /></a><figcaption>Barrios of Aguadilla</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Aguadilla is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ward_(electoral_subdivision)" title="Ward (electoral subdivision)">wards</a>). The municipal government buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in barrio Pueblo.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Aguacate,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguacate, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Aguacate</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguadilla barrio-pueblo">Aguadilla barrio-pueblo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arenales,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arenales, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Arenales</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Borinquen,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Borinquen, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Borinquen</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Caimital_Alto,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caimital Alto, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Caimital Alto</a></li>\n<li><a Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Camaceyes</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ceiba_Alta,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ceiba Alta, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Ceiba Alta</a></li>\n<li><a Rico">Corrales</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guerrero,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guerrero, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Guerrero</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maleza_Alta,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Maleza Alta, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Maleza Alta</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maleza_Baja,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Maleza Baja, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Maleza Baja</a></li>\n<li><a Puerto Rico">Palmar</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Victoria, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Victoria</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_barrios_and_sectors_of_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of barrios and sectors of Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">List of barrios and sectors of Aguadilla, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Via,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/La_Via%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-La_Via%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/La_Via%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-La_Via%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/La_Via%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-La_Via%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="442" /></a><figcaption>A structure is used for flood-control in <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Sector La Via</i></span>, a Special Community in Aguadilla.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in turn are further subdivided into smaller local populated place areas/units called <b>sectores</b> (which means <i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-sectores_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sectores-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Aguadilla: <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">El Palmar, Cerro Calero, Cerro Visbal, Cuesta Vieja, La V\xc3\xada</i></span>, and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Poblado San Antonio</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Temperature_of_sea">Temperature of sea</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Temperature of sea"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><a href="/wiki/Aguadilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Aguadilla">Aguadilla</a><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th><b>Jan</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Feb</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Mar</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Apr</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>May</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Jun</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Jul</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Aug</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Sep</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Oct</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Nov</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Dec</b>\n</th>\n<th><b>Year</b>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background: #CCFFCC; color: black;">77&#160;\xc2\xb0F (25&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CCFFCC; color: black;">75&#160;\xc2\xb0F (24&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CCFFCC; color: black;">77&#160;\xc2\xb0F (25&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CCFFCC; color: black;">77&#160;\xc2\xb0F (25&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CCFF99; color: black;">79&#160;\xc2\xb0F (26&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFF66; color: black;">81&#160;\xc2\xb0F (27&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFCC66; color: black;">84&#160;\xc2\xb0F (29&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFCC66; color: black;">84&#160;\xc2\xb0F (29&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFCC66; color: black;">86&#160;\xc2\xb0F (30&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFF66; color: black;">84&#160;\xc2\xb0F (29&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CCFF99; color: black;">82&#160;\xc2\xb0F (28&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CCFFCC; color: black;">79&#160;\xc2\xb0F (26&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #CCFF99; color: black;">78.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F (26.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguadilla_shopping_mall.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Aguadilla_shopping_mall.jpg/170px-Aguadilla_shopping_mall.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Aguadilla_shopping_mall.jpg/255px-Aguadilla_shopping_mall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Aguadilla_shopping_mall.jpg/340px-Aguadilla_shopping_mall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="324" /></a><figcaption>An entrance to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla_Mall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aguadilla Mall (page does not exist)">Aguadilla Mall</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The city is currently home to a variety of industrial and pharmaceutical plants such sa <a href="/wiki/LifeScan" title="LifeScan">LifeScan</a>, Symmetricom, <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hewlett_Packard_Enterprise" title="Hewlett Packard Enterprise">Hewlett Packard Enterprise</a>. Most of them are located at San Antonio Technological Park. The airport has <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Technik" title="Lufthansa Technik">Lufthansa Technik</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while others like Suiza Dairy, <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a> and Productos La Aguadillana are located in Camaseyes Industrial Park. Other industries that are based in Aguadilla are rubber, plastics, leather, textiles, steel, wood, machinery, and food processing.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_General_Info_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_General_Info-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The retail sector is another source of economy in Aguadilla. Shopping malls like Aguadilla Mall, Aguadilla Shopping Center, Aguadilla Town Center, and others are some of the main commercial and retail centers of the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo_03.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo_03.jpg/220px-Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo_03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo_03.jpg/330px-Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo_03.jpg/440px-Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3647" data-file-height="2735" /></a><figcaption>"Pintalto" project in Cerro Cabrera</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In 2018, <a href="/wiki/Suiza_Dairy" title="Suiza Dairy">Suiza Dairy</a>, a milk brand, opened a plant in Aguadilla at the cost of $40,000,000 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollars</a>. The plant is expected to earn $160,000,000 US dollars in the period form 2018 to 2038.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, Aguadilla received the City Livability Award from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Conference_of_Mayors" title="United States Conference of Mayors">United States Conference of Mayors</a> and honored the efforts spearheaded by Carlos M\xc3\xa9ndez Mart\xc3\xadnez. Specifically mentioned was "Pintalto", a project where Cerro Cabrero area, in the <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguadilla barrio-pueblo">downtown</a> area of Aguadilla was painted in rich, lively colors.<sup id="cite_ref-GmbH_2019_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GmbH_2019-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tourism">Tourism</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Schoolyards_Beach,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Schoolyards_Beach%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Schoolyards_Beach%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Schoolyards_Beach%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Schoolyards_Beach%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Schoolyards_Beach%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Schoolyards_Beach%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3539" data-file-height="1987" /></a><figcaption>Schoolyards Beach, surf spot in Aguadilla</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Aguadilla is part of the <a href="/wiki/Porta_del_Sol" title="Porta del Sol">Porta del Sol</a> touristic region in Puerto Rico. The Porta del Sol website highlights Aguadilla\'s beaches for <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources</a>, Aguadilla has the most beaches on the island, with nineteen in total.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some of the beaches are considered among the best for <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a>, like Surfer\'s Beach, <a href="/wiki/Gas_Chambers" title="Gas Chambers">Gas Chambers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crash_Boat_Beach" title="Crash Boat Beach">Crash Boat</a>, Wilderness, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Because of this, Aguadilla has served as host to surfing competitions, like the <a href="/wiki/International_Surfing_Association" title="International Surfing Association">ISA World Championship</a> in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other attractions of the town are <a href="/wiki/Las_Cascadas" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Cascadas">Las Cascadas Water Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_Ice_Skating_Arena" title="Aguadilla Ice Skating Arena">Aguadilla Ice Skating Arena</a>, which is the only <a href="/wiki/Ice_skating" title="Ice skating">ice skating</a> complex in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are nine places in Aguadilla listed on the US <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Old_Urban_Cemetery" title="Old Urban Cemetery">Old Urban Cemetery</a></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Piedra_(Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico)" title="Casa de Piedra (Aguadilla, Puerto Rico)">Casa de Piedra</a></i></span></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/District_Courthouse_(Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico)" title="District Courthouse (Aguadilla, Puerto Rico)">District Courthouse (Aguadilla, Puerto Rico)</a></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/El_Parterre" title="El Parterre">El Parterre, Ojo de Agua</a></i></span></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Punta_Borinquen_Light" title="Punta Borinquen Light">Punta Borinquen Light</a></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Fuerte_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="Fuerte de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n">Fuerte de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a></i></span></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_San_Carlos_Borromeo" title="Iglesia de San Carlos Borromeo">Iglesia de San Carlos Borromeo</a></i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 Church San Carlos Borromeo</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cardona_Residence" title="Cardona Residence">Cardona Residence</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%B3pez_Residence" title="L\xc3\xb3pez Residence">L\xc3\xb3pez Residence</a></li></ul>\n<p>Other places of interest in Aguadilla include:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1184024115"><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 20em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla_City_Hall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aguadilla City Hall (page does not exist)">Aguadilla City Hall</a> \xe2\x80\x93 originally built in 1918. Reconstructed after the <a href="/wiki/1918_San_Ferm%C3%ADn_earthquake" title="1918 San Ferm\xc3\xadn earthquake">1918 earthquake</a>.</li>\n<li>Banyan Treehouse \xe2\x80\x93 wooden house around a <a href="/wiki/Banyan" title="Banyan">banyan</a> tree (none of its parts touch the tree)</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Campanitas de Cristal</i></span>, a fountain</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cruz_de_Culebrinas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cruz de Culebrinas (page does not exist)">Christopher Columbus Monument</a> \xe2\x80\x93 a monument which consists of a cross originally made of marble, and had to be rebuilt after the earthquake.</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Parque_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Parque Crist\xc3\xb3bal Col\xc3\xb3n (page does not exist)">Parque Crist\xc3\xb3bal Col\xc3\xb3n</a></i></span>, a park</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">El Merendero</i></span></li>\n<li>Fisherman\'s Monument</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Jard\xc3\xadn del Atl\xc3\xa1ntico</i></span>, a square</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Las Cascadas</i></span> (The Waterfalls) Water Park (Closed after Hurricane Maria in 2017)</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Old_Sugar_Pier_of_Aguadilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Old Sugar Pier of Aguadilla (page does not exist)">Old Sugar Pier of Aguadilla</a></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Paseo Miguel Garcia M\xc3\xa9ndez</i></span></li>\n<li>Punta Borinquen Golf Course \xe2\x80\x93 an 18-hole golf course, originally built for President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Punta_Borinquen_Light" title="Punta Borinquen Light">Punta Borinquen Lighthouse</a> and ruins</li>\n<li>Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Monument</li>\n<li>Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Square</li>\n<li>Ramey Skate Park, a skatepark at the Ramey Military Base</li>\n<li>Youth Fountain at <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</i></span> Park</li></ul>\n</div>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Puerto_Rico" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico">COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign in 2021. The campaign featured a passport book with a page for each municipality. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Voy Turisteando</i></span> Aguadilla passport page lists Crash Boat Beach, Survival Beach, Rompeolas Beach, and Pe\xc3\xb1a Blanca Beach as places of interest for locals.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Beaches">Beaches</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Beaches"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Rompeolas_Bar_and_Grill,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/View_from_Rompeolas_Bar_and_Grill%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-View_from_Rompeolas_Bar_and_Grill%2C_Aguadilla%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="3527" data-file-height="2645" /></a><figcaption>View from Rompeolas Bar and Grill, at Rompeolas Beach in Aguadilla</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There are 32 beaches in Aguadilla.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some of the more well-known beaches include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Balneario Municipal de Aguadilla (GNIS ID 1990599)</li>\n<li>Playa La Ruina (GNIS ID 1991881) also called Wilderness Beach or <i>Las Ruinas</i> ("The Ruins" in English)<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Punta_Borinquen_Beach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Punta Borinquen Beach (page does not exist)">Playa Punta Borinquen</a> (GNIS ID 1991891)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Crash_Boat_Beach" title="Crash Boat Beach">Crash Boat Beach</a></li>\n<li>Survival Beach<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Surfer\'s Beach<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rompeolas_Beach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rompeolas Beach (page does not exist)">Rompeolas Beach</a> / Rompeolas Beach North also known as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Playa Tamarindo</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Aguadilla celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in October. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de San Carlos Borromeo</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_General_Info_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_General_Info-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Aguadilla include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Velorio de <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Reyes</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Celebrated mostly in January, they are a religious ceremony held as gratitude to the <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Magi" title="Biblical Magi">Three Kings</a> for some answered prayer. They usually consist of hymns, prayers, and other religious expressions.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Kite Festival \xe2\x80\x93 Held in April, it includes kiosks, music, and kite flying.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Fiestas San Antonio \xe2\x80\x93 April</li>\n<li>Verbena de Corrales \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Beach Festival \xe2\x80\x93 June<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Festival del <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">At\xc3\xban</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Celebrated in July, it is a festival dedicated to the fishing of the <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a>.</li>\n<li>Festival de la M\xc3\xbasica \xe2\x80\x93 July</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Aguadilla is home to several professional and amateur sports teams. The most notable are the Aguadilla Divas of the <a href="/wiki/Female_Superior_Volleyball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Female Superior Volleyball League">Female Superior Volleyball League</a>, and the Aguadilla Sharks of the <a href="/wiki/Superior_Baseball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Superior Baseball League">Superior Baseball League</a> (Double-A). The Divas play their home games in the <a href="/wiki/Luis_T._Diaz_Coliseum" title="Luis T. Diaz Coliseum">Luis T. D\xc3\xadaz Coliseum</a> in Downtown Aguadilla from January to March, while the Sharks play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Canena_Marquez_Stadium" title="Luis A. Canena Marquez Stadium">Luis A. Canena M\xc3\xa1rquez Stadium</a> from February to May.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Club\n</th>\n<th scope="col">League\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Sport\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Venue\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal; text-align: center;">Aguadilla Sharks\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Superior_Baseball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Superior Baseball League">Superior Baseball League</a>\n</td>\n<td>Baseball\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Canena_Marquez_Stadium" title="Luis A. Canena Marquez Stadium">Luis A. Canena M\xc3\xa1rquez Stadium</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal; text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_Divas" title="Aguadilla Divas">Aguadilla Divas</a>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Female_Superior_Volleyball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Female Superior Volleyball League">Female Superior Volleyball League</a>\n</td>\n<td>Volleyball\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Luis_T._Diaz_Coliseum" title="Luis T. Diaz Coliseum">Luis T. Diaz Coliseum</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Aguadilla also had a professional basketball team called the Aguadilla Sharks, that played for the <a href="/wiki/Baloncesto_Superior_Nacional" title="Baloncesto Superior Nacional">BSN</a> league. This team was merged into the <a href="/wiki/Cangrejeros_de_Santurce_(basketball)" title="Cangrejeros de Santurce (basketball)">Cangrejeros de Santurce</a> in 1998.\n</p><p>Aguadilla is also a place where many famous baseball players originate from. There are plans for a future <a href="/wiki/ECHL" title="ECHL">ECHL</a> Minor League Hockey franchise for the city.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Communication">Communication</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Communication"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Radio">Radio</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Radio"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/WABA_(AM)" title="WABA (AM)">WABA</a> WABA La Grande 850AM is located in Aguadilla.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WWNA" title="WWNA">WWNA</a> better known as Radio Una 1340AM is located in Aguadilla.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WVOZ_(AM)" title="WVOZ (AM)">WVOZ</a> WAPA Radio frequency 1580AM is located in Aguadilla.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Television">Television</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Television"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/WOLE-TV" class="mw-redirect" title="WOLE-TV">WOLE-TV</a> 12.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WELU" title="WELU">WELU</a> is a religious <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting" title="Broadcasting">broadcast</a> company.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WSJP-LD" class="mw-redirect" title="WSJP-LD">WSJP-LD</a> CW 18 is a <a href="/wiki/CW_Television_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="CW Television Network">CW Television Network</a> affiliated station.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 href="#cite_note-auto-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The 1887 census conducted by Spain showed Aguadilla had a population of 16,140.<sup id="cite_ref-1887_Census_by_Spain_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1887_Census_by_Spain-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the US 2010 Census, there were 60,949 people in the city. This represents a decrease of more than 3,000 from the 2000 Census.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 1,668.5 inhabitants per square mile (644.2/km<sup>2</sup>). The 2020 Census indicated the municipality has 55,101 residents representing a decline of over 5,000 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As a whole, Puerto Rico is populated mainly by people from <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a> or Spanish and European descent. Statistics taken from the 2000 census shows that 83.6% of Aguadillanos identify as having <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> or <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> origin, 5.0% are <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black</a>, 0.2% are <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a>, 0.2% <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a>, 0.1% <a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiian" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Hawaiian">Native Hawaiian</a>/<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">Pacific Islander</a>, 8.2% were some other race, and 2.8% two or more races.\n</p><p>In March 2012, unemployment was at 16.2%, which is the same percent it was in November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-radiografia2012_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radiografia2012-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religion">Religion</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236091366"><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Special:EditPage/Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Most Aguadillanos are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> with a majority being <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>. Like most cities in Puerto Rico Aguadilla has their Catholic church located on the main square in their downtown. There is also a significant community of <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a> including <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">Adventists</a>. Aguadilla has an <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> community with and Islamic Center located on <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_111" title="Puerto Rico Highway 111">PR-111</a> in <a href="/wiki/Palmar,_Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Palmar, Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Palmar</a> barrio.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="City">City</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: City"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>All municipalities in Puerto Rico are administered by a mayor, elected every four years. The current mayor of Aguadilla is Julio Rold\xc3\xa1n Concepci\xc3\xb3n, of the Popular Democratic Party (PPD).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="State">State</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: State"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Most state agencies are based at the Government Center Building with the exception of the <i>Corporaci\xc3\xb3n del Seguro del Estado</i> (State Insurance Agency) and the <i>Centro de Servicios al Conductor</i> (Driver\'s Services Center). Most state agencies left their offices after the Senatorial District was taken away from Aguadilla.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Public_safety">Public safety</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Public safety"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Aguadilla has its own police department, <i><a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_City_Police_Department" title="Aguadilla City Police Department">Polic\xc3\xada Municipal Aguadilla</a></i> (Aguadilla City Police Department), located in <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla_barrio-pueblo" title="Aguadilla barrio-pueblo">Aguadilla Pueblo</a>. The A.C.P.D. only has jurisdiction in the municipality of Aguadilla and provide service and protection to local citizens and travelers alike.\n</p><p>Aguadilla also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Police Department">Puerto Rico Police Department</a> Command for its Region. This region covers Aguada, Aguadilla, <a href="/wiki/Isabela,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isabela, Puerto Rico">Isabela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moca,_Puerto_Rico" title="Moca, Puerto Rico">Moca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinc%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Rinc\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Rinc\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a>. It also hosts the PRPD Highway Patrol Division for its region, the FURA Division of the PRPD, the <a href="/wiki/US_Army_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="US Army Reserve">US Army Reserve</a> Center, PR National Guard, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Coast_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Coast Guard">U.S. Coast Guard</a>, and the Border Patrol. It is also served by another PRPD station in San Antonio Village (Precinct 203 Ramey-San Antonio).\n</p><p>The city has a single correctional facility, <a href="/wiki/Guerrero_Correctional_Institution" title="Guerrero Correctional Institution">Guerrero Correctional Institution</a>, operated by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Corrections_and_Rehabilitation" title="Puerto Rico Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation">Puerto Rico Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation</a>.\n</p><p>In recent years, Aguadilla has seen an increase in Type I crimes, which include <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burglary" title="Burglary">burglary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Theft" title="Theft">theft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-radiografia2012_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radiografia2012-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="FBI_satellite_office">FBI satellite office</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: FBI satellite office"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There is an <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> satellite office located in Aguadilla.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mayors">Mayors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
